 A BILL FOR

  1 An Act prohibiting employers and employment agencies from
  2    seeking the criminal record or criminal history from
  3    applicants for employment under certain circumstances,
  4    establishing a criminal history employment application task
  5    force, providing penalties, and including effective date
  6    provisions.
  7 BE IT ENACTED BY THE GENERAL ASSEMBLY OF THE STATE OF IOWA:
    TLSB 1930YH (3) 87
    je/rj

PAG LIN

  1 28    Sec. 3.    1 27 report is filed.
  1 28    Sec. 3.    1 28    Sec. 3.    1 29    1.  The general assembly declares that:
  1 30    a.  Removing obstacles to employment for individuals with
  1 31 criminal records provides economic and social opportunities to
  1 32 a large group of individuals in Iowa, as well as increasing the
  1 33 productivity, health, and safety of Iowa communities.
  1 34    b.  Employment advertisements in Iowa frequently include
  1 35 language regarding criminal records that is unrelated to the
  2  1 employment vacancy and that either explicitly precludes or
  2  2 strongly dissuades individuals from applying for employment for
  2  3 which they are otherwise qualified.
  2  4    c.  Individuals with criminal records represent a group of
  2  5 job seekers ready and able to enlarge and contribute to the
  2  6 workforce.
  2  7    d.  Securing employment significantly reduces the risk of
  2  8 recidivism for individuals with criminal records.
  2  9    e.  The opportunity for individuals with criminal records
  2 10 to secure employment or to pursue, practice, or engage in
  2 11 a meaningful and profitable trade, occupation, vocation,
  2 12 profession, or business is essential to rehabilitation and
  2 13 their resumption of the responsibilities of citizenship.
  2 14    2.  It is the purpose of this chapter to improve the economic
  2 15 viability, health, and security of Iowa communities and to
  2 16 assist individuals with criminal records to reintegrate into
  2 17 the community, become productive members of the workforce, and
  2 18 provide for their families and themselves.

  2 19    Sec. 4.    2 19    Sec. 4.    2 20    1.  "Applicant" means a person pursuing employment with an
  2 21 employer or with or through an employment agency.
  2 22    2.  "Commissioner" means the labor commissioner, appointed
  2 23 pursuant to section 91.2, or the labor commissioner's designee.
  2 24    3.  "Criminal record or criminal history" means information
  2 25 collected or possessed by any criminal justice agency or
  2 26 judicial system in this state or in another jurisdiction,
  2 27 including a federal, military, tribal, or foreign jurisdiction,
  2 28 concerning individuals which information includes identifiable
  2 29 descriptions and notations of arrests, detentions, indictments,
  2 30 or other formal criminal charges, and any disposition arising
  2 31 therefrom, including acquittal, deferred judgment, sentencing,
  2 32 correctional supervision, release, or conviction, and any
  2 33 sentence arising from a verdict or plea of guilty or nolo
  2 34 contendere, including a sentence of incarceration, a suspended
  2 35 sentence, a sentence of probation, or a sentence of conditional
  3  1 discharge.
  3  2    4.  "Employer" means a person who has four or more employees
  3  3 in the current or preceding calendar year and includes an agent
  3  4 of such a person. For purposes of this chapter, individuals
  3  5 who are members of the employer's family shall not be counted
  3  6 as employees.
  3  7    5.  "Employment agency" means a person who, with or without
  3  8 compensation, regularly brings together those desiring to
  3  9 employ and those desiring employment and includes an agent of
  3 10 such a person.

  3 11    Sec. 5.    3 11    Sec. 5.    3 12 exceptions.
  3 13    1.  An employer or employment agency shall not inquire
  3 14 about or require disclosure of the criminal record or criminal
  3 15 history of an applicant until the applicant's interview is
  3 16 being conducted or, if an interview will not be conducted,
  3 17 until after a conditional offer of employment is made to the
  3 18 applicant by the employer or employment agency.
  3 19    2.  Subsection 1 does not apply to the following positions
  3 20 if an employer or employment agency establishes a separate
  3 21 application form for such positions that includes the title and
  3 22 job description of the position, the specific state or federal
  3 23 law or bonding requirement that applies to the position, and
  3 24 the types of criminal offenses that would preclude an applicant
  3 25 from being hired for the position:
  3 26    a.  Positions where employers are required to exclude
  3 27 applicants with certain criminal convictions from employment
  3 28 due to federal or state law.
  3 29    b.  Positions where a fidelity bond or an equivalent bond is
  3 30 required and an applicant's conviction of one or more specified
  3 31 criminal offenses would disqualify the applicant from obtaining
  3 32 such bond, in which case an employer may include a question or
  3 33 otherwise inquire whether the applicant has ever been convicted
  3 34 of such specified criminal offenses.
  3 35    3.  Subsection 1 does not prohibit an employer or employment
  4  1 agency from notifying applicants in writing of specific
  4  2 offenses that will disqualify an applicant from employment in a
  4  3 particular position as permitted by subsection 2.
  4  4    4.  Subsection 1 does not apply to the following positions:
  4  5    a.  Positions where an employee will work within the
  4  6 residence of the employer if the employer or members of the
  4  7 employer's family reside therein during such employment.
  4  8    b.  Positions where an employee will have entry access to a
  4  9 personal residence or an occupied unit in a multiple housing
  4 10 structure.
  4 11    c.  Positions where an employee will render personal service
  4 12 to the person of the employer or members of the employer's
  4 13 family.
  4 14    5.  An employment agency shall not be liable for a violation
  4 15 of subsection 1 if the employment agency can demonstrate by
  4 16 clear and convincing evidence that such violation was caused by
  4 17 the employment agency's good=faith reliance on an affirmative
  4 18 representation by an employer that one of the exceptions listed
  4 19 in subsection 2 or 4 applied to the position in question.  The
  4 20 employer shall be liable for any such violations.

  3 30 required and an applicant's conviction of one or more specified
  3 31 criminal offenses would disqualify the applicant from obtaining
  3 32 such bond, in which case an employer may include a question or
  3 33 otherwise inquire whether the applicant has ever been convicted
  3 34 of such specified criminal offenses.
  3 35    3.  Subsection 1 does not prohibit an employer or employment
  4  1 agency from notifying applicants in writing of specific
  4  2 offenses that will disqualify an applicant from employment in a
  4  3 particular position as permitted by subsection 2.
  4  4    4.  Subsection 1 does not apply to the following positions:
  4  5    a.  Positions where an employee will work within the
  4  6 residence of the employer if the employer or members of the
  4  7 employer's family reside therein during such employment.
  4  8    b.  Positions where an employee will have entry access to a
  4  9 personal residence or an occupied unit in a multiple housing
  4 10 structure.
  4 11    c.  Positions where an employee will render personal service
  4 12 to the person of the employer or members of the employer's
  4 13 family.
  4 14    5.  An employment agency shall not be liable for a violation
  4 15 of subsection 1 if the employment agency can demonstrate by
  4 16 clear and convincing evidence that such violation was caused by
  4 17 the employment agency's good=faith reliance on an affirmative
  4 18 representation by an employer that one of the exceptions listed
  4 19 in subsection 2 or 4 applied to the position in question.  The
  4 20 employer shall be liable for any such violations.

  4 11    c.  Positions where an employee will render personal service
  4 12 to the person of the employer or members of the employer's
  4 13 family.
  4 14    5.  An employment agency shall not be liable for a violation
  4 15 of subsection 1 if the employment agency can demonstrate by
  4 16 clear and convincing evidence that such violation was caused by
  4 17 the employment agency's good=faith reliance on an affirmative
  4 18 representation by an employer that one of the exceptions listed
  4 19 in subsection 2 or 4 applied to the position in question.  The
  4 20 employer shall be liable for any such violations.

  4 30    Sec. 7.    4 30    Sec. 7.    4 31    An employer or employment agency who violates the provisions
  4 32 of this chapter shall be subject to a penalty as follows:
  4 33    1.  For a first violation, the commissioner shall issue
  4 34 a    written warning to the employer or employment agency that
  4 35 includes notice regarding penalties for subsequent violations
  5  1 and the employer or employment agency shall have thirty days
  5  2 to remedy the violation.
  5  3    2.  For a second violation, or if a previous violation is not
  5  4 remedied within thirty days of notice by the commissioner, the
  5  5 commissioner may impose a civil penalty of up to five hundred
  5  6 dollars.
  5  7    3.  For a third violation, or if a previous violation is not
  5  8 remedied within sixty days of notice by the commissioner, the
  5  9 commissioner may impose a civil penalty of up to one thousand
  5 10 five hundred dollars.
  5 11    4.  For subsequent violations, or if a previous violation is
  5 12 not remedied within ninety days of notice by the commissioner,
  5 13 the commissioner may impose a civil penalty of up to one
  5 14 thousand five hundred dollars for every thirty days that pass
  5 15 thereafter without compliance.
  5 16    Sec. 8.    4 32 of this chapter shall be subject to a penalty as follows:

  5 16    Sec. 8.    5 16    Sec. 8.    5 17    1.  The commissioner may propose that an employer be assessed
  5 18 a civil penalty as provided in section 91F.4 by serving the
  5 19 employer with notice of such proposal in the same manner as an
  5 20 original notice is served under the rules of civil procedure.
  5 21 Upon service of such notice, the proposed assessment shall be
  5 22 treated as a contested case under chapter 17A.  However, an
  5 23 employer or employment agency must request a hearing within
  5 24 thirty days of being served.
  5 25    2.  If an employer or employment agency does not request
  5 26 a hearing pursuant to subsection 1 or if the commissioner
  5 27 determines, after an appropriate hearing, that an employer
  5 28 or employment agency is in violation of this chapter, the
  5 29 commissioner shall assess a civil penalty in accordance with
  5 30 section 91F.5.
  5 31    3.  An employer or employment agency may seek judicial
  5 32 review of any assessment made under subsection 2 by instituting
  5 33 proceedings for judicial review pursuant to chapter 17A.
  5 34  However, such proceedings must be instituted in the district
  5 35 court of the county in which the violation or one of the
  6  1 violations occurred and within thirty days of the day on which
  6  2 the employer was notified that an assessment has been made.
  6  3    4.  After the time for seeking judicial review has expired
  6  4 or after all judicial review has been exhausted and the
  6  5 commissioner's assessment has been upheld, the commissioner
  6  6 shall request the attorney general to recover the assessed
  6  7 penalties in a civil action.
  6  8    5.  Civil penalties recovered pursuant to this section shall
  6  9 be remitted by the commissioner to the treasurer of state for
  6 10 deposit in the general fund of the state.

  6  3    4.  After the time for seeking judicial review has expired
  6  4 or after all judicial review has been exhausted and the
  6  5 commissioner's assessment has been upheld, the commissioner
  6  6 shall request the attorney general to recover the assessed
  6  7 penalties in a civil action.
  6  8    5.  Civil penalties recovered pursuant to this section shall
  6  9 be remitted by the commissioner to the treasurer of state for
  6 10 deposit in the general fund of the state.
  6 11    Sec. 9.    5 20 original notice is served under the rules of civil procedure.
  5 21 Upon service of such notice, the proposed assessment shall be
  5 22 treated as a contested case under chapter 17A.  However, an
  5 23 employer or employment agency must request a hearing within
  5 24 thirty days of being served.
  5 25    2.  If an employer or employment agency does not request
  5 26 a hearing pursuant to subsection 1 or if the commissioner
  5 27 determines, after an appropriate hearing, that an employer
  5 28 or employment agency is in violation of this chapter, the
  5 29 commissioner shall assess a civil penalty in accordance with
  5 30 section 91F.5.
  5 31    3.  An employer or employment agency may seek judicial
  5 32 review of any assessment made under subsection 2 by instituting
  5 33 proceedings for judicial review pursuant to chapter 17A.
  5 34  However, such proceedings must be instituted in the district
  5 35 court of the county in which the violation or one of the
  6  1 violations occurred and within thirty days of the day on which
  6  2 the employer was notified that an assessment has been made.

  6  5 commissioner's assessment has been upheld, the commissioner

  6  7 penalties in a civil action.

  6 10 deposit in the general fund of the state.

  6 14    Sec. 10.  EFFECTIVE DATE.  This division of this Act takes
  6 15 effect January 1, 2018.
  6 16                           DIVISION II
  6 17       CRIMINAL HISTORY EMPLOYMENT APPLICATION TASK FORCE
  6 18    Sec. 11.  CRIMINAL HISTORY EMPLOYMENT APPLICATION TASK FORCE
  6 19 AND REPORT.
  6 20    1.  A criminal history employment application task force
  6 21 is created. The task force shall consist of the following
  6 22 members:
  6 23    a.  The labor commissioner or the labor commissioner's
  6 24 designee, who shall represent public sector employers.
  6 25    b.  Two representatives of established civil rights
  6 26 and civil liberties organizations appointed by the labor
  6 27 commissioner.
  6 28    c.  Two representatives of private sector employers
  6 29 appointed by the labor commissioner.
  6 30    d.  One representative of a private sector labor
  6 31 organization appointed by the labor commissioner.
  6 32    e.  One representative of a statewide public sector labor
  6 33 organization appointed by the labor commissioner.
  6 34    2.  The task force shall study appropriate voluntary
  6 35 standards and procedures for evaluating employment applications
  7  1 from an individual with a criminal history, including but not
  7  2 limited to the nature of the crime, the age at which the crime
  7  3 was committed, the nature of the duties of the position applied
  7  4 for, and relevant evidence of the individual's rehabilitation.
  7  5    3.  The labor services division of the department of
  7  6 workforce development shall provide staffing services for the
  7  7 task force. The labor commissioner or the labor commissioner's
  7  8 designee shall serve as the chairperson of the task force.
  7  9    4.  The members of the task force shall serve without
  7 10 compensation and shall not be reimbursed for their expenses.
  7 11    5.  The task force shall submit a report regarding its
  7 12 findings and recommendations to the governor and the general
  7 13 assembly no later than January 1, 2018. The report shall
  7 14 include a model pamphlet or other publication in both printed
  7 15 and electronic form on evaluating employment applications
  7 16 from individuals with criminal histories to be distributed to
  7 17 employers in Iowa in a manner similar to other information
  7 18 distributed by the labor commissioner.
  7 19    Sec. 12.  EFFECTIVE UPON ENACTMENT.  This division of this
  7 20 Act, being deemed of immediate importance, takes effect upon
  7 21 enactment.
  7 22                           EXPLANATION
  7 23 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  7 24 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  7 25    DIVISION I ==== PROHIBITED HIRING PRACTICES ==== CRIMINAL
  7 26 RECORD OR CRIMINAL HISTORY.  This bill prohibits an employer
  7 27 or employment agency from inquiring about or requiring
  7 28 disclosure of the criminal record or criminal history of an
  7 29 applicant until the applicant's interview is being conducted.
  7 30 If an interview for the position will not be conducted,
  7 31 the prohibition applies until after a conditional offer
  7 32 of employment is made to the applicant by the employer or
  7 33 employment agency.
  7 34    The prohibition does not apply to certain positions listed
  7 35 in the bill if an employer or employment agency establishes
  8  1 a separate application form for such positions that includes
  8  2 certain information listed in the bill. The bill does not
  8  3 prohibit an employer or employment agency from notifying
  8  4 applicants in writing of specific offenses that will disqualify
  8  5 an applicant from employment in a particular position as
  8  6 permitted by these exceptions.
  8  7    The prohibition does not apply to certain additional
  8  8 positions listed in the bill.
  8  9    An employment agency shall not be liable for a violation of
  8 10 the prohibition if the employment agency can demonstrate by
  8 11 clear and convincing evidence that such violation was caused by
  8 12 the employment agency's good=faith reliance on an affirmative
  8 13 representation by an employer that one of the exceptions listed
  8 14 in the bill applied to the position in question. The employer
  8 15 shall be liable for any such violations.
  8 16    The bill defines "applicant" as a person pursuing employment
  8 17 with an employer or with or through an employment agency.
  8 18 The bill defines "employer" as a person who has four or more
  8 19 employees in the current or preceding calendar year and an
  8 20 agent of such a person, excluding family members. The bill
  8 21 defines "employment agency" as a person who, with or without
  8 22 compensation, regularly brings together those desiring to
  8 23 employ and those desiring employment and an agent of such a
  8 24 person.
  8 25    The bill defines "criminal record or criminal history" as
  8 26 information collected or possessed by any criminal justice
  8 27 agency or judicial system in this state or in another
  8 28 jurisdiction, including a federal, military, tribal, or
  8 29 foreign jurisdiction, concerning individuals which information
  8 30 includes identifiable descriptions and notations of arrests,
  8 31 detentions, indictments, or other formal criminal charges,
  8 32 and any disposition arising therefrom, including acquittal,
  8 33 deferred judgment, sentencing, correctional supervision,
  8 34 release, or conviction, and any sentence arising from a verdict
  8 35 or plea of guilty or nolo contendere, including a sentence of
  9  1 incarceration, a suspended sentence, a sentence of probation,
  9  2 or a sentence of conditional discharge.
  9  3    An employer or employment agency that violates the
  9  4 provisions of the bill is subject to civil penalties ranging
  9  5 from a written warning for a first violation to up to $1,500
  9  6 every 30 days for a fourth or subsequent violation not remedied
  9  7 within 90 days.
  9  8    The labor commissioner may hold hearings and investigate
  9  9 alleged violations of the bill by an employer or employment
  9 10 agency, may assess and recover civil penalties and seek
  9 11 attorney general assistance in such recovery according to the
  9 12 procedural provisions of the bill, and shall adopt rules to
  9 13 administer the bill.
  9 14    Division I of the bill shall not be construed to require an
  9 15 employer to employ an individual with a criminal record.
  9 16    Division I of the bill takes effect January 1, 2018.
  9 17    DIVISION II ==== CRIMINAL HISTORY EMPLOYMENT APPLICATION TASK
  9 18 FORCE.  Division II of the bill creates a criminal history
  9 19 employment application task force. The task force shall study
  9 20 appropriate voluntary standards and procedures for evaluating
  9 21 employment applications from an individual with a criminal
  9 22 history, including but not limited to the nature of the crime,
  9 23 the age at which the crime was committed, the nature of the
  9 24 duties of the position applied for, and relevant evidence of
  9 25 the individual's rehabilitation.
  9 26    The bill lists the membership of the task force. The labor
  9 27 commissioner shall be the chairperson of the task force and
  9 28 the labor services division of the department of workforce
  9 29 development shall provide staffing services for the task force.
  9 30    The task force shall submit a report regarding its findings
  9 31 and recommendations to the governor and the general assembly no
  9 32 later than January 1, 2018. The report shall include a model
  9 33 pamphlet or other publication in both printed and electronic
  9 34 form on evaluating employment applications from individuals
  9 35 with criminal histories to be distributed to employers in Iowa
 10  1 in a manner similar to other information distributed by the
 10  2 labor commissioner.
 10  3    Division II of the bill takes effect upon enactment.
       LSB 1930YH (3) 87
       je/rj
  6 13 employ an individual with a criminal record.
  6 14    Sec. 10.  EFFECTIVE DATE.  This division of this Act takes
  6 15 effect January 1, 2018.
  6 16                           DIVISION II
  6 17       CRIMINAL HISTORY EMPLOYMENT APPLICATION TASK FORCE
  6 18    Sec. 11.  CRIMINAL HISTORY EMPLOYMENT APPLICATION TASK FORCE
  6 19 AND REPORT.
  6 20    1.  A criminal history employment application task force
  6 21 is created. The task force shall consist of the following
  6 22 members:
  6 23    a.  The labor commissioner or the labor commissioner's
  6 24 designee, who shall represent public sector employers.
  6 25    b.  Two representatives of established civil rights
  6 26 and civil liberties organizations appointed by the labor
  6 27 commissioner.
  6 28    c.  Two representatives of private sector employers
  6 29 appointed by the labor commissioner.
  6 30    d.  One representative of a private sector labor
  6 31 organization appointed by the labor commissioner.
  6 32    e.  One representative of a statewide public sector labor
  6 33 organization appointed by the labor commissioner.
  6 34    2.  The task force shall study appropriate voluntary
  6 35 standards and procedures for evaluating employment applications
  7  1 from an individual with a criminal history, including but not
  7  2 limited to the nature of the crime, the age at which the crime
  7  3 was committed, the nature of the duties of the position applied
  7  4 for, and relevant evidence of the individual's rehabilitation.
  7  5    3.  The labor services division of the department of
  7  6 workforce development shall provide staffing services for the
  7  7 task force. The labor commissioner or the labor commissioner's
  7  8 designee shall serve as the chairperson of the task force.
  7  9    4.  The members of the task force shall serve without
  7 10 compensation and shall not be reimbursed for their expenses.
  7 11    5.  The task force shall submit a report regarding its
  7 12 findings and recommendations to the governor and the general
  7 13 assembly no later than January 1, 2018. The report shall
  7 14 include a model pamphlet or other publication in both printed
  7 15 and electronic form on evaluating employment applications
  7 16 from individuals with criminal histories to be distributed to
  7 17 employers in Iowa in a manner similar to other information
  7 18 distributed by the labor commissioner.
  7 19    Sec. 12.  EFFECTIVE UPON ENACTMENT.  This division of this
  7 20 Act, being deemed of immediate importance, takes effect upon
  7 21 enactment.
  7 22                           EXPLANATION
  7 23 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  7 24 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  7 25    DIVISION I ==== PROHIBITED HIRING PRACTICES ==== CRIMINAL
  7 26 RECORD OR CRIMINAL HISTORY.  This bill prohibits an employer
  7 27 or employment agency from inquiring about or requiring
  7 28 disclosure of the criminal record or criminal history of an
  7 29 applicant until the applicant's interview is being conducted.
  7 30 If an interview for the position will not be conducted,
  7 31 the prohibition applies until after a conditional offer
  7 32 of employment is made to the applicant by the employer or
  7 33 employment agency.
  7 34    The prohibition does not apply to certain positions listed
  7 35 in the bill if an employer or employment agency establishes
  8  1 a separate application form for such positions that includes
  8  2 certain information listed in the bill. The bill does not
  8  3 prohibit an employer or employment agency from notifying
  8  4 applicants in writing of specific offenses that will disqualify
  8  5 an applicant from employment in a particular position as
  8  6 permitted by these exceptions.
  8  7    The prohibition does not apply to certain additional
  8  8 positions listed in the bill.
  8  9    An employment agency shall not be liable for a violation of
  8 10 the prohibition if the employment agency can demonstrate by
  8 11 clear and convincing evidence that such violation was caused by
  8 12 the employment agency's good=faith reliance on an affirmative
  8 13 representation by an employer that one of the exceptions listed
  8 14 in the bill applied to the position in question. The employer
  8 15 shall be liable for any such violations.
  8 16    The bill defines "applicant" as a person pursuing employment
  8 17 with an employer or with or through an employment agency.
  8 18 The bill defines "employer" as a person who has four or more
  8 19 employees in the current or preceding calendar year and an
  8 20 agent of such a person, excluding family members. The bill
  8 21 defines "employment agency" as a person who, with or without
  8 22 compensation, regularly brings together those desiring to
  8 23 employ and those desiring employment and an agent of such a
  8 24 person.
  8 25    The bill defines "criminal record or criminal history" as
  8 26 information collected or possessed by any criminal justice
  8 27 agency or judicial system in this state or in another
  8 28 jurisdiction, including a federal, military, tribal, or
  8 29 foreign jurisdiction, concerning individuals which information
  8 30 includes identifiable descriptions and notations of arrests,
  8 31 detentions, indictments, or other formal criminal charges,
  8 32 and any disposition arising therefrom, including acquittal,
  8 33 deferred judgment, sentencing, correctional supervision,
  8 34 release, or conviction, and any sentence arising from a verdict
  8 35 or plea of guilty or nolo contendere, including a sentence of
  9  1 incarceration, a suspended sentence, a sentence of probation,
  9  2 or a sentence of conditional discharge.
  9  3    An employer or employment agency that violates the
  9  4 provisions of the bill is subject to civil penalties ranging
  9  5 from a written warning for a first violation to up to $1,500
  9  6 every 30 days for a fourth or subsequent violation not remedied
  9  7 within 90 days.
  9  8    The labor commissioner may hold hearings and investigate
  9  9 alleged violations of the bill by an employer or employment
  9 10 agency, may assess and recover civil penalties and seek
  9 11 attorney general assistance in such recovery according to the
  9 12 procedural provisions of the bill, and shall adopt rules to
  9 13 administer the bill.
  9 14    Division I of the bill shall not be construed to require an
  9 15 employer to employ an individual with a criminal record.
  9 16    Division I of the bill takes effect January 1, 2018.
  9 17    DIVISION II ==== CRIMINAL HISTORY EMPLOYMENT APPLICATION TASK
  9 18 FORCE.  Division II of the bill creates a criminal history
  9 19 employment application task force. The task force shall study
  9 20 appropriate voluntary standards and procedures for evaluating
  9 21 employment applications from an individual with a criminal
  9 22 history, including but not limited to the nature of the crime,
  9 23 the age at which the crime was committed, the nature of the
  9 24 duties of the position applied for, and relevant evidence of
  9 25 the individual's rehabilitation.
  9 26    The bill lists the membership of the task force. The labor
  9 27 commissioner shall be the chairperson of the task force and
  9 28 the labor services division of the department of workforce
  9 29 development shall provide staffing services for the task force.
  9 30    The task force shall submit a report regarding its findings
  9 31 and recommendations to the governor and the general assembly no
  9 32 later than January 1, 2018. The report shall include a model
  9 33 pamphlet or other publication in both printed and electronic
  9 34 form on evaluating employment applications from individuals
  9 35 with criminal histories to be distributed to employers in Iowa
 10  1 in a manner similar to other information distributed by the
 10  2 labor commissioner.
 10  3    Division II of the bill takes effect upon enactment.
       LSB 1930YH (3) 87
       je/rj
  6 14    Sec. 10.  EFFECTIVE DATE.  This division of this Act takes
  6 15 effect January 1, 2018.
  6 16                           DIVISION II
  6 17       CRIMINAL HISTORY EMPLOYMENT APPLICATION TASK FORCE
  6 18    Sec. 11.  CRIMINAL HISTORY EMPLOYMENT APPLICATION TASK FORCE
  6 19 AND REPORT.
  6 20    1.  A criminal history employment application task force
  6 21 is created. The task force shall consist of the following
  6 22 members:
  6 23    a.  The labor commissioner or the labor commissioner's
  6 24 designee, who shall represent public sector employers.
  6 25    b.  Two representatives of established civil rights
  6 26 and civil liberties organizations appointed by the labor
  6 27 commissioner.
  6 28    c.  Two representatives of private sector employers
  6 29 appointed by the labor commissioner.
  6 30    d.  One representative of a private sector labor
  6 31 organization appointed by the labor commissioner.
  6 32    e.  One representative of a statewide public sector labor
  6 33 organization appointed by the labor commissioner.
  6 34    2.  The task force shall study appropriate voluntary
  6 35 standards and procedures for evaluating employment applications
  7  1 from an individual with a criminal history, including but not
  7  2 limited to the nature of the crime, the age at which the crime
  7  3 was committed, the nature of the duties of the position applied
  7  4 for, and relevant evidence of the individual's rehabilitation.
  7  5    3.  The labor services division of the department of
  7  6 workforce development shall provide staffing services for the
  7  7 task force. The labor commissioner or the labor commissioner's
  7  8 designee shall serve as the chairperson of the task force.
  7  9    4.  The members of the task force shall serve without
  7 10 compensation and shall not be reimbursed for their expenses.
  7 11    5.  The task force shall submit a report regarding its
  7 12 findings and recommendations to the governor and the general
  7 13 assembly no later than January 1, 2018. The report shall
  7 14 include a model pamphlet or other publication in both printed
  7 15 and electronic form on evaluating employment applications
  7 16 from individuals with criminal histories to be distributed to
  7 17 employers in Iowa in a manner similar to other information
  7 18 distributed by the labor commissioner.
  7 19    Sec. 12.  EFFECTIVE UPON ENACTMENT.  This division of this
  7 20 Act, being deemed of immediate importance, takes effect upon
  7 21 enactment.

  6 34    2.  The task force shall study appropriate voluntary
  6 35 standards and procedures for evaluating employment applications
  7  1 from an individual with a criminal history, including but not
  7  2 limited to the nature of the crime, the age at which the crime
  7  3 was committed, the nature of the duties of the position applied
  7  4 for, and relevant evidence of the individual's rehabilitation.
  7  5    3.  The labor services division of the department of
  7  6 workforce development shall provide staffing services for the
  7  7 task force. The labor commissioner or the labor commissioner's
  7  8 designee shall serve as the chairperson of the task force.
  7  9    4.  The members of the task force shall serve without
  7 10 compensation and shall not be reimbursed for their expenses.
  7 11    5.  The task force shall submit a report regarding its
  7 12 findings and recommendations to the governor and the general
  7 13 assembly no later than January 1, 2018. The report shall
  7 14 include a model pamphlet or other publication in both printed
  7 15 and electronic form on evaluating employment applications
  7 16 from individuals with criminal histories to be distributed to
  7 17 employers in Iowa in a manner similar to other information
  7 18 distributed by the labor commissioner.
  7 19    Sec. 12.  EFFECTIVE UPON ENACTMENT.  This division of this
  7 20 Act, being deemed of immediate importance, takes effect upon
  7 21 enactment.
  7 22                           EXPLANATION
  7 23 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  7 24 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  7 25    DIVISION I ==== PROHIBITED HIRING PRACTICES ==== CRIMINAL
  7 26 RECORD OR CRIMINAL HISTORY.  This bill prohibits an employer
  7 27 or employment agency from inquiring about or requiring
  7 28 disclosure of the criminal record or criminal history of an
  7 29 applicant until the applicant's interview is being conducted.
  7 30 If an interview for the position will not be conducted,
  7 31 the prohibition applies until after a conditional offer
  7 32 of employment is made to the applicant by the employer or
  7 33 employment agency.
  7 34    The prohibition does not apply to certain positions listed
  7 35 in the bill if an employer or employment agency establishes
  8  1 a separate application form for such positions that includes
  8  2 certain information listed in the bill. The bill does not
  8  3 prohibit an employer or employment agency from notifying
  8  4 applicants in writing of specific offenses that will disqualify
  8  5 an applicant from employment in a particular position as
  8  6 permitted by these exceptions.
  8  7    The prohibition does not apply to certain additional
  8  8 positions listed in the bill.
  8  9    An employment agency shall not be liable for a violation of
  8 10 the prohibition if the employment agency can demonstrate by
  8 11 clear and convincing evidence that such violation was caused by
  8 12 the employment agency's good=faith reliance on an affirmative
  8 13 representation by an employer that one of the exceptions listed
  8 14 in the bill applied to the position in question. The employer
  8 15 shall be liable for any such violations.
  8 16    The bill defines "applicant" as a person pursuing employment
  8 17 with an employer or with or through an employment agency.
  8 18 The bill defines "employer" as a person who has four or more
  8 19 employees in the current or preceding calendar year and an
  8 20 agent of such a person, excluding family members. The bill
  8 21 defines "employment agency" as a person who, with or without
  8 22 compensation, regularly brings together those desiring to
  8 23 employ and those desiring employment and an agent of such a
  8 24 person.
  8 25    The bill defines "criminal record or criminal history" as
  8 26 information collected or possessed by any criminal justice
  8 27 agency or judicial system in this state or in another
  8 28 jurisdiction, including a federal, military, tribal, or
  8 29 foreign jurisdiction, concerning individuals which information
  8 30 includes identifiable descriptions and notations of arrests,
  8 31 detentions, indictments, or other formal criminal charges,
  8 32 and any disposition arising therefrom, including acquittal,
  8 33 deferred judgment, sentencing, correctional supervision,
  8 34 release, or conviction, and any sentence arising from a verdict
  8 35 or plea of guilty or nolo contendere, including a sentence of
  9  1 incarceration, a suspended sentence, a sentence of probation,
  9  2 or a sentence of conditional discharge.
  9  3    An employer or employment agency that violates the
  9  4 provisions of the bill is subject to civil penalties ranging
  9  5 from a written warning for a first violation to up to $1,500
  9  6 every 30 days for a fourth or subsequent violation not remedied
  9  7 within 90 days.
  9  8    The labor commissioner may hold hearings and investigate
  9  9 alleged violations of the bill by an employer or employment
  9 10 agency, may assess and recover civil penalties and seek
  9 11 attorney general assistance in such recovery according to the
  9 12 procedural provisions of the bill, and shall adopt rules to
  9 13 administer the bill.
  9 14    Division I of the bill shall not be construed to require an
  9 15 employer to employ an individual with a criminal record.
  9 16    Division I of the bill takes effect January 1, 2018.
  9 17    DIVISION II ==== CRIMINAL HISTORY EMPLOYMENT APPLICATION TASK
  9 18 FORCE.  Division II of the bill creates a criminal history
  9 19 employment application task force. The task force shall study
  9 20 appropriate voluntary standards and procedures for evaluating
  9 21 employment applications from an individual with a criminal
  9 22 history, including but not limited to the nature of the crime,
  9 23 the age at which the crime was committed, the nature of the
  9 24 duties of the position applied for, and relevant evidence of
  9 25 the individual's rehabilitation.
  9 26    The bill lists the membership of the task force. The labor
  9 27 commissioner shall be the chairperson of the task force and
  9 28 the labor services division of the department of workforce
  9 29 development shall provide staffing services for the task force.
  9 30    The task force shall submit a report regarding its findings
  9 31 and recommendations to the governor and the general assembly no
  9 32 later than January 1, 2018. The report shall include a model
  9 33 pamphlet or other publication in both printed and electronic
  9 34 form on evaluating employment applications from individuals
  9 35 with criminal histories to be distributed to employers in Iowa
 10  1 in a manner similar to other information distributed by the
 10  2 labor commissioner.
 10  3    Division II of the bill takes effect upon enactment.
       LSB 1930YH (3) 87
       je/rj
  6 18    Sec. 11.  CRIMINAL HISTORY EMPLOYMENT APPLICATION TASK FORCE
  6 19 AND REPORT.
  6 20    1.  A criminal history employment application task force
  6 21 is created. The task force shall consist of the following
  6 22 members:
  6 23    a.  The labor commissioner or the labor commissioner's
  6 24 designee, who shall represent public sector employers.
  6 25    b.  Two representatives of established civil rights
  6 26 and civil liberties organizations appointed by the labor
  6 27 commissioner.
  6 28    c.  Two representatives of private sector employers
  6 29 appointed by the labor commissioner.
  6 30    d.  One representative of a private sector labor
  6 31 organization appointed by the labor commissioner.
  6 32    e.  One representative of a statewide public sector labor
  6 33 organization appointed by the labor commissioner.
  6 34    2.  The task force shall study appropriate voluntary
  6 35 standards and procedures for evaluating employment applications
  7  1 from an individual with a criminal history, including but not
  7  2 limited to the nature of the crime, the age at which the crime
  7  3 was committed, the nature of the duties of the position applied
  7  4 for, and relevant evidence of the individual's rehabilitation.
  7  5    3.  The labor services division of the department of
  7  6 workforce development shall provide staffing services for the
  7  7 task force. The labor commissioner or the labor commissioner's
  7  8 designee shall serve as the chairperson of the task force.
  7  9    4.  The members of the task force shall serve without
  7 10 compensation and shall not be reimbursed for their expenses.
  7 11    5.  The task force shall submit a report regarding its
  7 12 findings and recommendations to the governor and the general
  7 13 assembly no later than January 1, 2018. The report shall
  7 14 include a model pamphlet or other publication in both printed
  7 15 and electronic form on evaluating employment applications
  7 16 from individuals with criminal histories to be distributed to
  7 17 employers in Iowa in a manner similar to other information
  7 18 distributed by the labor commissioner.
  7 19    Sec. 12.  EFFECTIVE UPON ENACTMENT.  This division of this
  7 20 Act, being deemed of immediate importance, takes effect upon
  7 21 enactment.

  7 25    DIVISION I ==== PROHIBITED HIRING PRACTICES ==== CRIMINAL
  7 26 RECORD OR CRIMINAL HISTORY.  This bill prohibits an employer
  7 27 or employment agency from inquiring about or requiring
  7 28 disclosure of the criminal record or criminal history of an
  7 29 applicant until the applicant's interview is being conducted.
  7 30 If an interview for the position will not be conducted,
  7 31 the prohibition applies until after a conditional offer
  7 32 of employment is made to the applicant by the employer or
  7 33 employment agency.
  7 34    The prohibition does not apply to certain positions listed
  7 35 in the bill if an employer or employment agency establishes
  8  1 a separate application form for such positions that includes
  8  2 certain information listed in the bill. The bill does not
  8  3 prohibit an employer or employment agency from notifying
  8  4 applicants in writing of specific offenses that will disqualify
  8  5 an applicant from employment in a particular position as
  8  6 permitted by these exceptions.
  8  7    The prohibition does not apply to certain additional
  8  8 positions listed in the bill.
  8  9    An employment agency shall not be liable for a violation of
  8 10 the prohibition if the employment agency can demonstrate by
  8 11 clear and convincing evidence that such violation was caused by
  8 12 the employment agency's good=faith reliance on an affirmative
  8 13 representation by an employer that one of the exceptions listed
  8 14 in the bill applied to the position in question. The employer
  8 15 shall be liable for any such violations.
  8 16    The bill defines "applicant" as a person pursuing employment
  8 17 with an employer or with or through an employment agency.
  8 18 The bill defines "employer" as a person who has four or more
  8 19 employees in the current or preceding calendar year and an
  8 20 agent of such a person, excluding family members. The bill
  8 21 defines "employment agency" as a person who, with or without
  8 22 compensation, regularly brings together those desiring to
  8 23 employ and those desiring employment and an agent of such a
  8 24 person.
  8 25    The bill defines "criminal record or criminal history" as
  8 26 information collected or possessed by any criminal justice
  8 27 agency or judicial system in this state or in another
  8 28 jurisdiction, including a federal, military, tribal, or
  8 29 foreign jurisdiction, concerning individuals which information
  8 30 includes identifiable descriptions and notations of arrests,
  8 31 detentions, indictments, or other formal criminal charges,
  8 32 and any disposition arising therefrom, including acquittal,
  8 33 deferred judgment, sentencing, correctional supervision,
  8 34 release, or conviction, and any sentence arising from a verdict
  8 35 or plea of guilty or nolo contendere, including a sentence of
  9  1 incarceration, a suspended sentence, a sentence of probation,
  9  2 or a sentence of conditional discharge.
  9  3    An employer or employment agency that violates the
  9  4 provisions of the bill is subject to civil penalties ranging
  9  5 from a written warning for a first violation to up to $1,500
  9  6 every 30 days for a fourth or subsequent violation not remedied
  9  7 within 90 days.
  9  8    The labor commissioner may hold hearings and investigate
  9  9 alleged violations of the bill by an employer or employment
  9 10 agency, may assess and recover civil penalties and seek
  9 11 attorney general assistance in such recovery according to the
  9 12 procedural provisions of the bill, and shall adopt rules to
  9 13 administer the bill.
  9 14    Division I of the bill shall not be construed to require an
  9 15 employer to employ an individual with a criminal record.
  9 16    Division I of the bill takes effect January 1, 2018.
  9 17    DIVISION II ==== CRIMINAL HISTORY EMPLOYMENT APPLICATION TASK
  9 18 FORCE.  Division II of the bill creates a criminal history
  9 19 employment application task force. The task force shall study
  9 20 appropriate voluntary standards and procedures for evaluating
  9 21 employment applications from an individual with a criminal
  9 22 history, including but not limited to the nature of the crime,
  9 23 the age at which the crime was committed, the nature of the
  9 24 duties of the position applied for, and relevant evidence of
  9 25 the individual's rehabilitation.
  9 26    The bill lists the membership of the task force. The labor
  9 27 commissioner shall be the chairperson of the task force and
  9 28 the labor services division of the department of workforce
  9 29 development shall provide staffing services for the task force.
  9 30    The task force shall submit a report regarding its findings
  9 31 and recommendations to the governor and the general assembly no
  9 32 later than January 1, 2018. The report shall include a model
  9 33 pamphlet or other publication in both printed and electronic
  9 34 form on evaluating employment applications from individuals
  9 35 with criminal histories to be distributed to employers in Iowa
 10  1 in a manner similar to other information distributed by the
 10  2 labor commissioner.
 10  3    Division II of the bill takes effect upon enactment.
       LSB 1930YH (3) 87
       je/rj
  6 22 members:
  6 23    a.  The labor commissioner or the labor commissioner's
  6 24 designee, who shall represent public sector employers.
  6 25    b.  Two representatives of established civil rights
  6 26 and civil liberties organizations appointed by the labor
  6 27 commissioner.
  6 28    c.  Two representatives of private sector employers
  6 29 appointed by the labor commissioner.
  6 30    d.  One representative of a private sector labor
  6 31 organization appointed by the labor commissioner.
  6 32    e.  One representative of a statewide public sector labor
  6 33 organization appointed by the labor commissioner.
  6 34    2.  The task force shall study appropriate voluntary
  6 35 standards and procedures for evaluating employment applications
  7  1 from an individual with a criminal history, including but not
  7  2 limited to the nature of the crime, the age at which the crime
  7  3 was committed, the nature of the duties of the position applied
  7  4 for, and relevant evidence of the individual's rehabilitation.
  7  5    3.  The labor services division of the department of
  7  6 workforce development shall provide staffing services for the
  7  7 task force. The labor commissioner or the labor commissioner's
  7  8 designee shall serve as the chairperson of the task force.
  7  9    4.  The members of the task force shall serve without
  7 10 compensation and shall not be reimbursed for their expenses.
  7 11    5.  The task force shall submit a report regarding its
  7 12 findings and recommendations to the governor and the general
  7 13 assembly no later than January 1, 2018. The report shall
  7 14 include a model pamphlet or other publication in both printed
  7 15 and electronic form on evaluating employment applications
  7 16 from individuals with criminal histories to be distributed to
  7 17 employers in Iowa in a manner similar to other information
  7 18 distributed by the labor commissioner.
  7 19    Sec. 12.  EFFECTIVE UPON ENACTMENT.  This division of this
  7 20 Act, being deemed of immediate importance, takes effect upon
  7 21 enactment.

  8 34 release, or conviction, and any sentence arising from a verdict
  8 35 or plea of guilty or nolo contendere, including a sentence of
  9  1 incarceration, a suspended sentence, a sentence of probation,
  9  2 or a sentence of conditional discharge.
  9  3    An employer or employment agency that violates the
  9  4 provisions of the bill is subject to civil penalties ranging
  9  5 from a written warning for a first violation to up to $1,500
  9  6 every 30 days for a fourth or subsequent violation not remedied
  9  7 within 90 days.
  9  8    The labor commissioner may hold hearings and investigate
  9  9 alleged violations of the bill by an employer or employment
  9 10 agency, may assess and recover civil penalties and seek
  9 11 attorney general assistance in such recovery according to the
  9 12 procedural provisions of the bill, and shall adopt rules to
  9 13 administer the bill.
  9 14    Division I of the bill shall not be construed to require an
  9 15 employer to employ an individual with a criminal record.
  9 16    Division I of the bill takes effect January 1, 2018.
  9 17    DIVISION II ==== CRIMINAL HISTORY EMPLOYMENT APPLICATION TASK
  9 18 FORCE.  Division II of the bill creates a criminal history
  9 19 employment application task force. The task force shall study
  9 20 appropriate voluntary standards and procedures for evaluating
  9 21 employment applications from an individual with a criminal
  9 22 history, including but not limited to the nature of the crime,
  9 23 the age at which the crime was committed, the nature of the
  9 24 duties of the position applied for, and relevant evidence of
  9 25 the individual's rehabilitation.
  9 26    The bill lists the membership of the task force. The labor
  9 27 commissioner shall be the chairperson of the task force and
  9 28 the labor services division of the department of workforce
  9 29 development shall provide staffing services for the task force.
  9 30    The task force shall submit a report regarding its findings
  9 31 and recommendations to the governor and the general assembly no
  9 32 later than January 1, 2018. The report shall include a model
  9 33 pamphlet or other publication in both printed and electronic
  9 34 form on evaluating employment applications from individuals
  9 35 with criminal histories to be distributed to employers in Iowa
 10  1 in a manner similar to other information distributed by the
 10  2 labor commissioner.
 10  3    Division II of the bill takes effect upon enactment.
       LSB 1930YH (3) 87
       je/rj
  6 26 and civil liberties organizations appointed by the labor
  6 27 commissioner.
  6 28    c.  Two representatives of private sector employers
  6 29 appointed by the labor commissioner.
  6 30    d.  One representative of a private sector labor
  6 31 organization appointed by the labor commissioner.
  6 32    e.  One representative of a statewide public sector labor
  6 33 organization appointed by the labor commissioner.
  6 34    2.  The task force shall study appropriate voluntary
  6 35 standards and procedures for evaluating employment applications
  7  1 from an individual with a criminal history, including but not
  7  2 limited to the nature of the crime, the age at which the crime
  7  3 was committed, the nature of the duties of the position applied
  7  4 for, and relevant evidence of the individual's rehabilitation.
  7  5    3.  The labor services division of the department of
  7  6 workforce development shall provide staffing services for the
  7  7 task force. The labor commissioner or the labor commissioner's
  7  8 designee shall serve as the chairperson of the task force.
  7  9    4.  The members of the task force shall serve without
  7 10 compensation and shall not be reimbursed for their expenses.
  7 11    5.  The task force shall submit a report regarding its
  7 12 findings and recommendations to the governor and the general
  7 13 assembly no later than January 1, 2018. The report shall
  7 14 include a model pamphlet or other publication in both printed
  7 15 and electronic form on evaluating employment applications
  7 16 from individuals with criminal histories to be distributed to
  7 17 employers in Iowa in a manner similar to other information
  7 18 distributed by the labor commissioner.
  7 19    Sec. 12.  EFFECTIVE UPON ENACTMENT.  This division of this
  7 20 Act, being deemed of immediate importance, takes effect upon
  7 21 enactment.
  7 22                           EXPLANATION
  7 23 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  7 24 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  7 25    DIVISION I ==== PROHIBITED HIRING PRACTICES ==== CRIMINAL
  7 26 RECORD OR CRIMINAL HISTORY.  This bill prohibits an employer
  7 27 or employment agency from inquiring about or requiring
  7 28 disclosure of the criminal record or criminal history of an
  7 29 applicant until the applicant's interview is being conducted.
  7 30 If an interview for the position will not be conducted,
  7 31 the prohibition applies until after a conditional offer
  7 32 of employment is made to the applicant by the employer or
  7 33 employment agency.
  7 34    The prohibition does not apply to certain positions listed
  7 35 in the bill if an employer or employment agency establishes
  8  1 a separate application form for such positions that includes
  8  2 certain information listed in the bill. The bill does not
  8  3 prohibit an employer or employment agency from notifying
  8  4 applicants in writing of specific offenses that will disqualify
  8  5 an applicant from employment in a particular position as
  8  6 permitted by these exceptions.
  8  7    The prohibition does not apply to certain additional
  8  8 positions listed in the bill.
  8  9    An employment agency shall not be liable for a violation of
  8 10 the prohibition if the employment agency can demonstrate by
  8 11 clear and convincing evidence that such violation was caused by
  8 12 the employment agency's good=faith reliance on an affirmative
  8 13 representation by an employer that one of the exceptions listed
  8 14 in the bill applied to the position in question. The employer
  8 15 shall be liable for any such violations.
  8 16    The bill defines "applicant" as a person pursuing employment
  8 17 with an employer or with or through an employment agency.
  8 18 The bill defines "employer" as a person who has four or more
  8 19 employees in the current or preceding calendar year and an
  8 20 agent of such a person, excluding family members. The bill
  8 21 defines "employment agency" as a person who, with or without
  8 22 compensation, regularly brings together those desiring to
  8 23 employ and those desiring employment and an agent of such a
  8 24 person.
  8 25    The bill defines "criminal record or criminal history" as
  8 26 information collected or possessed by any criminal justice
  8 27 agency or judicial system in this state or in another
  8 28 jurisdiction, including a federal, military, tribal, or
  8 29 foreign jurisdiction, concerning individuals which information
  8 30 includes identifiable descriptions and notations of arrests,
  8 31 detentions, indictments, or other formal criminal charges,
  8 32 and any disposition arising therefrom, including acquittal,
  8 33 deferred judgment, sentencing, correctional supervision,
  8 34 release, or conviction, and any sentence arising from a verdict
  8 35 or plea of guilty or nolo contendere, including a sentence of
  9  1 incarceration, a suspended sentence, a sentence of probation,
  9  2 or a sentence of conditional discharge.
  9  3    An employer or employment agency that violates the
  9  4 provisions of the bill is subject to civil penalties ranging
  9  5 from a written warning for a first violation to up to $1,500
  9  6 every 30 days for a fourth or subsequent violation not remedied
  9  7 within 90 days.
  9  8    The labor commissioner may hold hearings and investigate
  9  9 alleged violations of the bill by an employer or employment
  9 10 agency, may assess and recover civil penalties and seek
  9 11 attorney general assistance in such recovery according to the
  9 12 procedural provisions of the bill, and shall adopt rules to
  9 13 administer the bill.
  9 14    Division I of the bill shall not be construed to require an
  9 15 employer to employ an individual with a criminal record.
  9 16    Division I of the bill takes effect January 1, 2018.
  9 17    DIVISION II ==== CRIMINAL HISTORY EMPLOYMENT APPLICATION TASK
  9 18 FORCE.  Division II of the bill creates a criminal history
  9 19 employment application task force. The task force shall study
  9 20 appropriate voluntary standards and procedures for evaluating
  9 21 employment applications from an individual with a criminal
  9 22 history, including but not limited to the nature of the crime,
  9 23 the age at which the crime was committed, the nature of the
  9 24 duties of the position applied for, and relevant evidence of
  9 25 the individual's rehabilitation.
  9 26    The bill lists the membership of the task force. The labor
  9 27 commissioner shall be the chairperson of the task force and
  9 28 the labor services division of the department of workforce
  9 29 development shall provide staffing services for the task force.
  9 30    The task force shall submit a report regarding its findings
  9 31 and recommendations to the governor and the general assembly no
  9 32 later than January 1, 2018. The report shall include a model
  9 33 pamphlet or other publication in both printed and electronic
  9 34 form on evaluating employment applications from individuals
  9 35 with criminal histories to be distributed to employers in Iowa
 10  1 in a manner similar to other information distributed by the
 10  2 labor commissioner.
 10  3    Division II of the bill takes effect upon enactment.
       LSB 1930YH (3) 87

  7  1 from an individual with a criminal history, including but not
  7  2 limited to the nature of the crime, the age at which the crime

  7  4 for, and relevant evidence of the individual's rehabilitation.
  7  5    3.  The labor services division of the department of

  7  7 task force. The labor commissioner or the labor commissioner's
  7  8 designee shall serve as the chairperson of the task force.

  7 10 compensation and shall not be reimbursed for their expenses.

  7 10 compensation and shall not be reimbursed for their expenses.
  7 11    5.  The task force shall submit a report regarding its
  7 12 findings and recommendations to the governor and the general
  7 13 assembly no later than January 1, 2018. The report shall
  7 14 include a model pamphlet or other publication in both printed
  7 15 and electronic form on evaluating employment applications
  7 16 from individuals with criminal histories to be distributed to
  7 17 employers in Iowa in a manner similar to other information
  7 18 distributed by the labor commissioner.
  7 19    Sec. 12.  EFFECTIVE UPON ENACTMENT.  This division of this
  7 20 Act, being deemed of immediate importance, takes effect upon
  7 21 enactment.
  7 22                           EXPLANATION
  7 23 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  7 24 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  7 25    DIVISION I ==== PROHIBITED HIRING PRACTICES ==== CRIMINAL
  7 26 RECORD OR CRIMINAL HISTORY.  This bill prohibits an employer
  7 27 or employment agency from inquiring about or requiring
  7 28 disclosure of the criminal record or criminal history of an
  7 29 applicant until the applicant's interview is being conducted.
  7 30 If an interview for the position will not be conducted,
  7 31 the prohibition applies until after a conditional offer
  7 32 of employment is made to the applicant by the employer or
  7 33 employment agency.
  7 34    The prohibition does not apply to certain positions listed
  7 35 in the bill if an employer or employment agency establishes
  8  1 a separate application form for such positions that includes
  8  2 certain information listed in the bill. The bill does not
  8  3 prohibit an employer or employment agency from notifying
  8  4 applicants in writing of specific offenses that will disqualify
  8  5 an applicant from employment in a particular position as
  8  6 permitted by these exceptions.
  8  7    The prohibition does not apply to certain additional
  8  8 positions listed in the bill.
  8  9    An employment agency shall not be liable for a violation of
  8 10 the prohibition if the employment agency can demonstrate by
  8 11 clear and convincing evidence that such violation was caused by
  8 12 the employment agency's good=faith reliance on an affirmative
  8 13 representation by an employer that one of the exceptions listed
  8 14 in the bill applied to the position in question. The employer
  8 15 shall be liable for any such violations.
  8 16    The bill defines "applicant" as a person pursuing employment
  8 17 with an employer or with or through an employment agency.
  8 18 The bill defines "employer" as a person who has four or more
  8 19 employees in the current or preceding calendar year and an
  8 20 agent of such a person, excluding family members. The bill
  8 21 defines "employment agency" as a person who, with or without
  8 22 compensation, regularly brings together those desiring to
  8 23 employ and those desiring employment and an agent of such a
  8 24 person.
  8 25    The bill defines "criminal record or criminal history" as
  8 26 information collected or possessed by any criminal justice
  8 27 agency or judicial system in this state or in another
  8 28 jurisdiction, including a federal, military, tribal, or
  8 29 foreign jurisdiction, concerning individuals which information
  8 30 includes identifiable descriptions and notations of arrests,
  8 31 detentions, indictments, or other formal criminal charges,
  8 32 and any disposition arising therefrom, including acquittal,
  8 33 deferred judgment, sentencing, correctional supervision,
  8 34 release, or conviction, and any sentence arising from a verdict
  8 35 or plea of guilty or nolo contendere, including a sentence of
  9  1 incarceration, a suspended sentence, a sentence of probation,
  9  2 or a sentence of conditional discharge.
  9  3    An employer or employment agency that violates the
  9  4 provisions of the bill is subject to civil penalties ranging
  9  5 from a written warning for a first violation to up to $1,500
  9  6 every 30 days for a fourth or subsequent violation not remedied
  9  7 within 90 days.
  9  8    The labor commissioner may hold hearings and investigate
  9  9 alleged violations of the bill by an employer or employment
  9 10 agency, may assess and recover civil penalties and seek
  9 11 attorney general assistance in such recovery according to the
  9 12 procedural provisions of the bill, and shall adopt rules to
  9 13 administer the bill.
  9 14    Division I of the bill shall not be construed to require an
  9 15 employer to employ an individual with a criminal record.
  9 16    Division I of the bill takes effect January 1, 2018.
  9 17    DIVISION II ==== CRIMINAL HISTORY EMPLOYMENT APPLICATION TASK
  9 18 FORCE.  Division II of the bill creates a criminal history
  9 19 employment application task force. The task force shall study
  9 20 appropriate voluntary standards and procedures for evaluating
  9 21 employment applications from an individual with a criminal
  9 22 history, including but not limited to the nature of the crime,
  9 23 the age at which the crime was committed, the nature of the
  9 24 duties of the position applied for, and relevant evidence of
  9 25 the individual's rehabilitation.
  9 26    The bill lists the membership of the task force. The labor
  9 27 commissioner shall be the chairperson of the task force and
  9 28 the labor services division of the department of workforce
  9 29 development shall provide staffing services for the task force.
  9 30    The task force shall submit a report regarding its findings
  9 31 and recommendations to the governor and the general assembly no
  9 32 later than January 1, 2018. The report shall include a model
  9 33 pamphlet or other publication in both printed and electronic
  9 34 form on evaluating employment applications from individuals
  9 35 with criminal histories to be distributed to employers in Iowa
 10  1 in a manner similar to other information distributed by the
 10  2 labor commissioner.
 10  3    Division II of the bill takes effect upon enactment.
       LSB 1930YH (3) 87
       je/rj
  6 31 organization appointed by the labor commissioner.
  6 32    e.  One representative of a statewide public sector labor
  6 33 organization appointed by the labor commissioner.
  6 34    2.  The task force shall study appropriate voluntary
  6 35 standards and procedures for evaluating employment applications
  7  1 from an individual with a criminal history, including but not
  7  2 limited to the nature of the crime, the age at which the crime
  7  3 was committed, the nature of the duties of the position applied
  7  4 for, and relevant evidence of the individual's rehabilitation.
  7  5    3.  The labor services division of the department of
  7  6 workforce development shall provide staffing services for the
  7  7 task force. The labor commissioner or the labor commissioner's
  7  8 designee shall serve as the chairperson of the task force.
  7  9    4.  The members of the task force shall serve without
  7 10 compensation and shall not be reimbursed for their expenses.
  7 11    5.  The task force shall submit a report regarding its
  7 12 findings and recommendations to the governor and the general
  7 13 assembly no later than January 1, 2018. The report shall
  7 14 include a model pamphlet or other publication in both printed
  7 15 and electronic form on evaluating employment applications
  7 16 from individuals with criminal histories to be distributed to
  7 17 employers in Iowa in a manner similar to other information
  7 18 distributed by the labor commissioner.
  7 19    Sec. 12.  EFFECTIVE UPON ENACTMENT.  This division of this
  7 20 Act, being deemed of immediate importance, takes effect upon
  7 21 enactment.

  9 14    Division I of the bill shall not be construed to require an
  9 15 employer to employ an individual with a criminal record.
  9 16    Division I of the bill takes effect January 1, 2018.
  9 17    DIVISION II ==== CRIMINAL HISTORY EMPLOYMENT APPLICATION TASK
  9 18 FORCE.  Division II of the bill creates a criminal history
  9 19 employment application task force. The task force shall study
  9 20 appropriate voluntary standards and procedures for evaluating
  9 21 employment applications from an individual with a criminal
  9 22 history, including but not limited to the nature of the crime,
  9 23 the age at which the crime was committed, the nature of the
  9 24 duties of the position applied for, and relevant evidence of
  9 25 the individual's rehabilitation.
  9 26    The bill lists the membership of the task force. The labor
  9 27 commissioner shall be the chairperson of the task force and
  9 28 the labor services division of the department of workforce
  9 29 development shall provide staffing services for the task force.
  9 30    The task force shall submit a report regarding its findings
  9 31 and recommendations to the governor and the general assembly no
  9 32 later than January 1, 2018. The report shall include a model
  9 33 pamphlet or other publication in both printed and electronic
  9 34 form on evaluating employment applications from individuals
  9 35 with criminal histories to be distributed to employers in Iowa
 10  1 in a manner similar to other information distributed by the
 10  2 labor commissioner.
 10  3    Division II of the bill takes effect upon enactment.
       LSB 1930YH (3) 87
       je/rj
  6 35 standards and procedures for evaluating employment applications
  7  1 from an individual with a criminal history, including but not
  7  2 limited to the nature of the crime, the age at which the crime
  7  3 was committed, the nature of the duties of the position applied
  7  4 for, and relevant evidence of the individual's rehabilitation.
  7  5    3.  The labor services division of the department of
  7  6 workforce development shall provide staffing services for the
  7  7 task force. The labor commissioner or the labor commissioner's
  7  8 designee shall serve as the chairperson of the task force.
  7  9    4.  The members of the task force shall serve without
  7 10 compensation and shall not be reimbursed for their expenses.
  7 11    5.  The task force shall submit a report regarding its
  7 12 findings and recommendations to the governor and the general
  7 13 assembly no later than January 1, 2018. The report shall
  7 14 include a model pamphlet or other publication in both printed
  7 15 and electronic form on evaluating employment applications
  7 16 from individuals with criminal histories to be distributed to
  7 17 employers in Iowa in a manner similar to other information
  7 18 distributed by the labor commissioner.

  7 20 Act, being deemed of immediate importance, takes effect upon
  7 21 enactment.
  7 22                           EXPLANATION
  7 23 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  7 24 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  7 25    DIVISION I ==== PROHIBITED HIRING PRACTICES ==== CRIMINAL
  7 26 RECORD OR CRIMINAL HISTORY.  This bill prohibits an employer
  7 27 or employment agency from inquiring about or requiring
  7 28 disclosure of the criminal record or criminal history of an
  7 29 applicant until the applicant's interview is being conducted.
  7 30 If an interview for the position will not be conducted,
  7 31 the prohibition applies until after a conditional offer
  7 32 of employment is made to the applicant by the employer or
  7 33 employment agency.
  7 34    The prohibition does not apply to certain positions listed
  7 35 in the bill if an employer or employment agency establishes
  8  1 a separate application form for such positions that includes
  8  2 certain information listed in the bill. The bill does not
  8  3 prohibit an employer or employment agency from notifying
  8  4 applicants in writing of specific offenses that will disqualify
  8  5 an applicant from employment in a particular position as
  8  6 permitted by these exceptions.
  8  7    The prohibition does not apply to certain additional
  8  8 positions listed in the bill.
  8  9    An employment agency shall not be liable for a violation of
  8 10 the prohibition if the employment agency can demonstrate by
  8 11 clear and convincing evidence that such violation was caused by
  8 12 the employment agency's good=faith reliance on an affirmative
  8 13 representation by an employer that one of the exceptions listed
  8 14 in the bill applied to the position in question. The employer
  8 15 shall be liable for any such violations.
  8 16    The bill defines "applicant" as a person pursuing employment
  8 17 with an employer or with or through an employment agency.
  8 18 The bill defines "employer" as a person who has four or more
  8 19 employees in the current or preceding calendar year and an
  8 20 agent of such a person, excluding family members. The bill
  8 21 defines "employment agency" as a person who, with or without
  8 22 compensation, regularly brings together those desiring to
  8 23 employ and those desiring employment and an agent of such a
  8 24 person.
  8 25    The bill defines "criminal record or criminal history" as
  8 26 information collected or possessed by any criminal justice
  8 27 agency or judicial system in this state or in another
  8 28 jurisdiction, including a federal, military, tribal, or
  8 29 foreign jurisdiction, concerning individuals which information
  8 30 includes identifiable descriptions and notations of arrests,
  8 31 detentions, indictments, or other formal criminal charges,
  8 32 and any disposition arising therefrom, including acquittal,
  8 33 deferred judgment, sentencing, correctional supervision,
  8 34 release, or conviction, and any sentence arising from a verdict
  8 35 or plea of guilty or nolo contendere, including a sentence of
  9  1 incarceration, a suspended sentence, a sentence of probation,
  9  2 or a sentence of conditional discharge.
  9  3    An employer or employment agency that violates the
  9  4 provisions of the bill is subject to civil penalties ranging
  9  5 from a written warning for a first violation to up to $1,500
  9  6 every 30 days for a fourth or subsequent violation not remedied
  9  7 within 90 days.
  9  8    The labor commissioner may hold hearings and investigate
  9  9 alleged violations of the bill by an employer or employment
  9 10 agency, may assess and recover civil penalties and seek
  9 11 attorney general assistance in such recovery according to the
  9 12 procedural provisions of the bill, and shall adopt rules to
  9 13 administer the bill.
  9 14    Division I of the bill shall not be construed to require an
  9 15 employer to employ an individual with a criminal record.
  9 16    Division I of the bill takes effect January 1, 2018.
  9 17    DIVISION II ==== CRIMINAL HISTORY EMPLOYMENT APPLICATION TASK
  9 18 FORCE.  Division II of the bill creates a criminal history
  9 19 employment application task force. The task force shall study
  9 20 appropriate voluntary standards and procedures for evaluating
  9 21 employment applications from an individual with a criminal
  9 22 history, including but not limited to the nature of the crime,
  9 23 the age at which the crime was committed, the nature of the
  9 24 duties of the position applied for, and relevant evidence of
  9 25 the individual's rehabilitation.
  9 26    The bill lists the membership of the task force. The labor
  9 27 commissioner shall be the chairperson of the task force and
  9 28 the labor services division of the department of workforce
  9 29 development shall provide staffing services for the task force.
  9 30    The task force shall submit a report regarding its findings
  9 31 and recommendations to the governor and the general assembly no
  9 32 later than January 1, 2018. The report shall include a model
  9 33 pamphlet or other publication in both printed and electronic
  9 34 form on evaluating employment applications from individuals
  9 35 with criminal histories to be distributed to employers in Iowa
 10  1 in a manner similar to other information distributed by the
 10  2 labor commissioner.
 10  3    Division II of the bill takes effect upon enactment.
       LSB 1930YH (3) 87

  7  2 limited to the nature of the crime, the age at which the crime
  7  3 was committed, the nature of the duties of the position applied
  7  4 for, and relevant evidence of the individual's rehabilitation.
  7  5    3.  The labor services division of the department of
  7  6 workforce development shall provide staffing services for the
  7  7 task force. The labor commissioner or the labor commissioner's
  7  8 designee shall serve as the chairperson of the task force.
  7  9    4.  The members of the task force shall serve without
  7 10 compensation and shall not be reimbursed for their expenses.
  7 11    5.  The task force shall submit a report regarding its
  7 12 findings and recommendations to the governor and the general
  7 13 assembly no later than January 1, 2018. The report shall
  7 14 include a model pamphlet or other publication in both printed
  7 15 and electronic form on evaluating employment applications
  7 16 from individuals with criminal histories to be distributed to
  7 17 employers in Iowa in a manner similar to other information
  7 18 distributed by the labor commissioner.

  7 20 Act, being deemed of immediate importance, takes effect upon
  7 21 enactment.
